  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_05916141-9e07-4614-b94f-9724827bd96d'
      });
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer5228026117867993107">The fantastic land of Amara is recovering from years of war inflicted on its citizens by outside forces-as well as from the spiritual apathy corroding the Amarans' hearts. With Kale and her father serving as dragon keepers for Paladin, the dragon populace has exploded. It's a peaceful, exciting time of rebuilding. And yet, an insidious, unseen evil lurks just beneath the s</span>
  <span id="freeText5228026117867993107" style="display:none">The fantastic land of Amara is recovering from years of war inflicted on its citizens by outside forces-as well as from the spiritual apathy corroding the Amarans' hearts. With Kale and her father serving as dragon keepers for Paladin, the dragon populace has exploded. It's a peaceful, exciting time of rebuilding. And yet, an insidious, unseen evil lurks just beneath the surface of the idyllic countryside. <b>
  <br />
</b><br /><b>Truth has never been more important, nor so difficult to discern. </b><br /><br />As Kale and her father are busy hatching, bonding, and releasing the younger generation of dragons as helpers throughout the kingdom, the light wizard has little time to develop her skills. Her husband, Sir Bardon-despite physical limitations resulting from his bout with the stakes disease-has become a leader, serving on the governing board under Paladin. When Kale and Bardon set aside their daily responsibilities to join meech dragons Regidor and Gilda on a quest to find a hidden meech colony, they encounter sinister forces. Their world is under attack by a secret enemy... can they overcome the ominous peril they can't even see?<br /><br />Prepare to experience breathtaking adventure and mind-blowing fantasy as never before in this dazzling, beautifully-crafted conclusion to Donita K. Paul's popular DragonKeeper Chronicles fantasy series.</span>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/46813996-darin">Darin</a>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">It depends on what dragons you are talking about. I believe that Mrs. Paul is giving the impression here that all dragons were initially good, but som<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">It depends on what dragons you are talking about. I believe that Mrs. Paul is giving the impression here that all dragons were initially good, but some have become evil; probably a bit of a reference to Genesis. So yes, dragons are good, and bad.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<div id="review_155691008" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/155691008" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5054531-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1301418988p2/5054531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/155691008?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/5054531-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5054531-becky?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5054531-becky?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5054531-becky?shelf=dragon">dragon</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer155691008" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12238789930747978500">I want to love these books, I really do. I've found so much to like in each of them, but I just can't get past the heavy-handed preaching. In this last one we find out that it's not just wrong to disagree with the mainstream religion, diversity of thought is more evil than a mountain-sized, man-eating dragon. I find that kind of message more terrifying than the lackluster villains in these books. Evidently, it's ok to look and act differently, as long as your beliefs fall in line with the "corre</span>
  <span id="freeText12238789930747978500" style="display:none">I want to love these books, I really do. I've found so much to like in each of them, but I just can't get past the heavy-handed preaching. In this last one we find out that it's not just wrong to disagree with the mainstream religion, diversity of thought is more evil than a mountain-sized, man-eating dragon. I find that kind of message more terrifying than the lackluster villains in these books. Evidently, it's ok to look and act differently, as long as your beliefs fall in line with the "correct" principles.<br /><br />It is certainly possible for evil men to use religion to lead people into death and destruction, but that is the risk you take when you allow people to choose for themselves. I prefer a world where we are still free to choose our own thoughts and beliefs, even if your idea of God is radically different from mine. I respect your beliefs and expect you to respect mine. It seems that this author feels differently and that bothered me and constantly stood between me and the story.<br /><br />As for the story itself, it's passable. I enjoyed the baby elements and the new kind of dragon was nifty. I thought the ending was flat and predictable. It's not a bad book, just a flawed one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12238789930747978500" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17621918042436778121">Some of you have probably heard of the Dragon Keeper Chronicles Series by Donita Paul. It is an amazing series that currently has 5 books in it - DragonSpell DragonQuest DragonKnight DragonFire DragonLight We enter the world of Amara with Knights, Wizards, Dragons and of course clear lines drawn between good and evil.   <span id="freeText17621918042436778121" style="display:none">Some of you have probably heard of the Dragon Keeper Chronicles Series by Donita Paul. It is an amazing series that currently has 5 books in it - DragonSpell DragonQuest DragonKnight DragonFire DragonLight We enter the world of Amara with Knights, Wizards, Dragons and of course clear lines drawn between good and evil. Donita has created many kinds of creatures and other amazing characters that take us through many adventures. One of my favorite parts is definitely the dragons themselves. There are different kinds with different gifts usually based on what color they are. They each have different personalities and are quite captivating really. This is a world that will pull you in and have you begging for more. I was a little behind the times with this series - I came in on book #5 (DragonLight) but was able to get the first one and read it before reading DragonLight. I loved them both and have since gotten the middle three and can't wait to go back to Amara and follow those journeys! This is a series written for YA but designed for anyone that likes fantasy and using their imaginations...</span>

  <span id="freeText16704298658706406714" style="display:none">A fantastic conclusion to the series!!<br />I've honestly enjoyed this series so much. At first, I was slightly put off by the dragons because all the dragons that have featured in the books I've read have been evil, but here there were good dragons. And boy, did I fall in love with them! Each of them were unique and fun to read about. <br />This novel tackled a different enemy than the former novels. This time the enemy came from 'within' and dealt with themes of compromise and deceit, which I think was well-done. <br />I loved stepping back into the wonderful creation that is Amara, and throughout the whole series, I've enjoyed every minute I've spent in there. <br />I was delighted to catch up with my favourite characters, especially Kale and Bardon. They are so cute together and it was so good to see the husband and wife duo working together. <br />With fun adventures, fascinating creatures, and magical inventions, this novel is not to be missed!<br />I would recommend this to lovers of Christian fantasy. </span>

<div id="review_33884820" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/33884820" />
    <a title="Robert" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/838731-robert"><img alt="Robert" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539983069p2/838731.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/33884820?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robert" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robert" href="/user/show/838731-robert">Robert</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/838731-robert?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer33884820&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer33884820" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3789479786741909569">I have to say, this final installment was the weakest in the series. Let me tell you why:<br/><br/>Donita introduces two menaces:<br/><br/>The Followers, a cult of Wulder extremists, and An ancient evil dragon named Mot Angara of truly mountainous (literally) size. Both of these are great threats to the Amarans: one trying to establish a dictatorial theocracy, and the other threatening to destroy the world.<br/><br/>Here's how they were dealt with:<br/><br/>While the Followers seemed a great menace, and seemed like they would be a tru</span>
  <span id="freeText3789479786741909569" style="display:none">I have to say, this final installment was the weakest in the series. Let me tell you why:<br /><br />Donita introduces two menaces:<br /><br />The Followers, a cult of Wulder extremists, and An ancient evil dragon named Mot Angara of truly mountainous (literally) size. Both of these are great threats to the Amarans: one trying to establish a dictatorial theocracy, and the other threatening to destroy the world.<br /><br />Here's how they were dealt with:<br /><br />While the Followers seemed a great menace, and seemed like they would be a true bane on the land and might actually win out, they are suddenly, quickly, and easily dealt with, and barely even blip on the events we actually see. It all happens "off screen", and those events barely even affect the story we do get to see, which is Mot Angara.<br /><br />Now, Mot Angara is a true terror, of ancient terror. We get a lot of background into the history of the various dragons, learn a great deal about the Meech, and see a lot of events that makes everything more difficult for the characters and truly makes you wonder how they will succeed. It creates a lot of tension that I enjoyed. But then, at the end, I felt cheated. The best way I can describe it, without giving away the ending, is as a gamer: Imagin playing a roleplaying game where you spend months building up and preparing your characters to face the great villain at the end, but then that villain is so powerful that you can't defeat it despite all your preparations, and so the DM has to intercede with an uber powerful NPC in order to give the story a "Happy Ending". I was very let down by the ending of this book.<br /><br />Also, I realized that the characters have a double standard, it seems. In the last book, they were ready to kick a valuable party member out of their group because he expressed opinions that the faith of the main characters isn't the only faith in the world, and that all of these faiths contained similar themes. In this book, another character, who shows less value in my opinion, frequently makes statements that to the others should be blasphemous, statements that outright deny that their god Wulder has any true power, and yet they tolerate it as all "misguided talk" and that this character has "had a rough past, and so they;re lack of faith is understandable". The double standard is so obvious and powerful that it upset me on many levels.<br /><br />Now, with all that said, the build up throughout the books was very good, and I did greatly enjoy reading about the adventure. If you have read the others, this one is definitely worth reading, but in my opinion, don't expect it to feel like a Grand Finale, because to me it fell short of that distinction.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3789479786741909569" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_841757040" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/841757040" />
    <a title="MC" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28164369-mc"><img alt="MC" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483779945p2/28164369.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/841757040?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="MC" class="user" itemprop="url" name="MC" href="/user/show/28164369-mc">MC</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8345435-dragonlight">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer841757040" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4922590236401561574">Very rarely have I been more disappointed with any story than I was with <i>DragonLight</i> by Donita K. Paul. This final volume in her popular five-book <i>Dragon Keeper Chronicles</i> series had such a promising plot, and such an unfortunately bad follow-through.<br/><br/>To summarize the plot without giving too much away, there is a cult growing in the land of Amara. This group, called "the Followers" seeks to subvert the teachings of Wulder, the one-true Creator and God, and also to exterminate the dragon populatio</span>
  <span id="freeText4922590236401561574" style="display:none">Very rarely have I been more disappointed with any story than I was with <i>DragonLight</i> by Donita K. Paul. This final volume in her popular five-book <i>Dragon Keeper Chronicles</i> series had such a promising plot, and such an unfortunately bad follow-through.<br /><br />To summarize the plot without giving too much away, there is a cult growing in the land of Amara. This group, called "the Followers" seeks to subvert the teachings of Wulder, the one-true Creator and God, and also to exterminate the dragon population. At the same time, there is an infestation of poisonous, finger- to hand-sized dragons that spit fire and seem to attack Dragon Keepers on sight. These evil little creatures seem to be tied to a legendary evil dragon called Mot Angra. These two plot threads are tied, obviously, and in some very clever and unique ways. That is the most that I can reveal without spoiling too much. All that I can say is that this is easily the worst book that Paul wrote, as she really did have a brilliant story, but horrible delivery.<br /><br />I will only highlight a few problems I had with the book. First of all, the involvement of Wulder for a literal <i>Deus ex Machina</i> was fine, except for it being really badly executed. The vessel that Wulder used, little Toopka from the earlier tales, and the revelations of her history that many may have expected, seemed forced and not shown in a convincing manner. She goes from being problematic in her lack of trust of those around her, to suddenly trusting and loving everyone always. It just had no believability and conflicted with her portrayals and characterization in earlier books.<br /><br />Then there is the issue of Paladin and his actions/words. The guy was always a tad of a wooden figure, but he always had some life to him, and during the story line from the previous book with his illness and recovery, he seemed to have even more life and dynamism. In this book, it's as if Paul preferred him as <i>less</i> emotional and <i>less</i> dynamic. I don't get why. In this book, he sounded annoying and caused many an eye-roll.<br /><br />Some might say it was his virtues and quoting of the fictional "Tomes" (which mirrored real-life lessons from the real Scriptures that Paul wanted to teach) that made him boring to me. I disagree for a few reasons. First of all, as I said, these were not always boring traits in previous books, especially the last one. Secondly, Bardon and others that have had similar quotes and virtues in the books haven't irritated me at all. I think that why I found Paladin irritating is that he wasn't the dynamic, normal sounding character the others were, but he sounded like some cheesy super-hero from the Silver Age of Comics/Cartoons, uttering really absurd lines. I half-expected him to tell the bad guys that they "can't defeat the Amaran Super-Friends" or something equally cringe-worthy.<br /><br />Finally, there is the issue of Toopka, and, well, just Toopka. I know she was always that way except for a period where she served Wulder, so of course her change makes sense. But another character's reaction to it? I'm sorry, but "yuck!"<br /><br />This book was a sore disappointment to me. I recommend you at least skim it to learn of the ending of the series, but please don't waste your money on this one. Get it from the library instead. I doubt you would want to read it again. I have so much respect for Mrs. Paul, who got me into the genre of Christian fantasy that I didn't really know was as big as it is and is growing to be. This is hard, but I must give my honest opinion. The rest of the series was great, as is <i>The Dragons of Chiril</i> series, but this one book was awful.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4922590236401561574" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_956592672" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/956592672" />
    <a title="Morgan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22315959-morgan"><img alt="Morgan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560270396p2/22315959.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/956592672?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Morgan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Morgan" href="/user/show/22315959-morgan">Morgan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22315959-morgan?shelf=outread-aubrey-2014">outread-aubrey-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer956592672" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2720125574890855328">The Dragon Keeper Chronicles has taken me on a delightful journey that sadly has finally come to an end. Well, it hasn't really come to an end. I still have the last two books from the library and keep picking them up and rereading my favorite bits. DragonLight was a worthy continuation that I greatly enjoyed, and I'm sad to have to say goodbye to Kale and Bardon.<br/><br/>Writing: 4/5<br/><br/>The writing is really pretty much the same as always. I suppose I can mention here the flaws in her climaxes. Donita K. Pa</span>
  <span id="freeText2720125574890855328" style="display:none">The Dragon Keeper Chronicles has taken me on a delightful journey that sadly has finally come to an end. Well, it hasn't really come to an end. I still have the last two books from the library and keep picking them up and rereading my favorite bits. DragonLight was a worthy continuation that I greatly enjoyed, and I'm sad to have to say goodbye to Kale and Bardon.<br /><br />Writing: 4/5<br /><br />The writing is really pretty much the same as always. I suppose I can mention here the flaws in her climaxes. Donita K. Paul is excellent at worldbuilding and character development. I mean fantastically excellent. And she weaves it all together like a master. But when it comes to climaxes, it just could really be better. The climax of DragonLight was rather anticlimactic. It so deserved to be epic and amazing, but it fell short. That being said, her writing did pull me into the story and make me sympathize with the characters.<br /><br />Setting: 5/5<br /><br />If you've been following these reviews, you already know how much I love Amara, so I won't bore you by reiterating it yet again. In this book you get to see the origins of the dragons, which was extremely interesting. I love how she weaves in further worldbuilding with every story in a way that interests the reader and never feels like an info dump.<br /><br />Plot: 4/5<br /><br />I really did enjoy the whole book. There were several plots woven through. One involves the cult of the Followers. It was very well done, and the allegorical meanings of it really stood out to me. The way they solved the problem did happen somewhat offscreen in a way that was easy to miss, so that's my only complaint about it. It really made me think about how easy it is to fall into the traps of those who wish to deceive.<br /><br />Then there was the whole thing about finding the meech colony. That became the main plot as...well, spoilers. But I loved how they gradually discovered the reason behind the attacks of the little black dragons and how it led into the climax. It was a bit anticlimactic and abrupt, the way it ended, but I still loved it. There's also Toopka's story, related to that, but I won't spoil it. To be honest, I'm not sure I understand it well enough to spoil it.<br /><br />Then there's the personal side of the story. SPOILER Kale has a baby! END SPOILER I loved seeing Kale and Bardon together. They're so entertaining, and it was great to see them move on to the next stage of their lives in this book.<br /><br />Character Development: 5/5<br /><br />Again, excellent. Gilda was a very well drawn character, and thoroughly aggravating. Seriously, when she found out that the aforesaid spoiler was going to happen, she was angry about it and made me mad. Bardon. *sniff* It was so sad to see him still struggling with stiffness from the stakes (a childhood disease dangerous in adulthood) that he had in the last book. I wanted so bad for him to be healed completely. No more spoilers, I won't say the conclusion of that. Kale was quite interesting in this book, due to the previous spoiler (my anti spoiler sister gave it to me before I read the book, so maybe it's not such a big one, but it isn't revealed until about halfway through the book). She was sometimes grumpy, and sometimes quite not, but I really enjoyed reading about her. Toopka was extra interesting, so was Sittiponder, and, really, the characters are just fantastic!<br /><br />Despite my struggles to get truly interested in the Dragon Keeper Chronicles at the beginning of the series, by the end I loved it, and highly recommend it to fantasy lovers. I only wish there were more books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2720125574890855328" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_308542158" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/308542158" />
    <a title="Valerie (Val&#39;s Vicinity)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8561323-valerie-val-s-vicinity"><img alt="Valerie (Val&#39;s Vicinity)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1334385833p2/8561323.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/308542158?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Valerie (Val&#39;s Vicinity)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Valerie (Val&#39;s Vicinity)" href="/user/show/8561323-valerie-val-s-vicinity">Valerie (Val&#39;s Vicinity)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer308542158" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4938620688648031732">Having read the whole series and comparing each book, I think I liked the storylines here in DragonLight the best out of the entire series. The quest for the meech colony was interesting and quite different from the storylines of the previous books. It was also interesting to see how things played out with the introduction of the "Followers", who in many (unfortunate) ways seem like a modern day cult. Kale and Bardon's attention and efforts focus on both of these storylines through-out the book.</span>
  <span id="freeText4938620688648031732" style="display:none">Having read the whole series and comparing each book, I think I liked the storylines here in DragonLight the best out of the entire series. The quest for the meech colony was interesting and quite different from the storylines of the previous books. It was also interesting to see how things played out with the introduction of the "Followers", who in many (unfortunate) ways seem like a modern day cult. Kale and Bardon's attention and efforts focus on both of these storylines through-out the book.<br /><br />Some thoughts on the series as a whole:<br />The DragonKeeper Chronicles isn't quite my normal reading genre, but I purchased the whole series for a bargain price about a year ago. When I got around to reading the books, unfortunately I ended up getting a bit burnt-out on the series somewhere around book 3. Maybe it would have been better if I hadn't read all 5 books back-to-back, but that's what I did. The 1st and 2nd held my attention well enough, but I really had to push myself through 3 and 4. This book, DragonLight (the 5th &amp; final in the series), recaptured my attention for the most part, but I still felt anxious to be done. As a result, I have to say that I'm glad to be done with the series at this point.<br /><br />The series is not a "kids-only" thing, the allegory within can speak to people of all ages. As a whole, I think younger-readers will probably get the most enjoyment from the series, but I can definitely see adults reading it as well. It would be a good series for families to read together, especially looking at it as a sort of teaching tool and discussion starter for the allegory and hidden truths. Dragon's and quests just aren't my normal genre, and I think that's probably most of the issue I had with it not always holding my attention.<br /><br />In closing, for DragonLight as a whole, I'd like to say 3.5 stars, but that's not an option... so I'll give it 4 stars since in my opinion DragonLight was a big improvement over the previous 2 books. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4938620688648031732" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_777716675" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/777716675" />
    <a title="Gloria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9576361-gloria"><img alt="Gloria" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/777716675?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gloria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gloria" href="/user/show/9576361-gloria">Gloria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone; fantasy lovers; dragon aficionados</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9576361-gloria?shelf=duncan-ga">duncan-ga</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9576361-gloria?shelf=hardcopy">hardcopy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9576361-gloria?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9576361-gloria?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer777716675" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4672417564828350961">DragonLight begins sometime after the events of DragonFire, but we are not told how long ago those events were.<br/><br/>There are several enemies and insidious purposes revealed in this book as well as some delightful surprises and restorations.<br/><br/>I really liked how they all stay together and most of the time worked together to resolve the issues that sprung up. I know a prior book, had a lot of "Wulder's principles", and while this book has a lot of them as well, they seem more put into practice then just </span>
  <span id="freeText4672417564828350961" style="display:none">DragonLight begins sometime after the events of DragonFire, but we are not told how long ago those events were.<br /><br />There are several enemies and insidious purposes revealed in this book as well as some delightful surprises and restorations.<br /><br />I really liked how they all stay together and most of the time worked together to resolve the issues that sprung up. I know a prior book, had a lot of "Wulder's principles", and while this book has a lot of them as well, they seem more put into practice then just spoken of. There's a particular scene where Barden gives advice to a husband who seems disrespectful of his wife, and it's wrapped up in one of the insidious purposes, so that Barton's advice is not only to help the household run harmoniously but also to keep this particular family out of the clutches of a cult. Sadly his advice in one aspect goes on unheeded, for we meet them later in the book.<br /><br />There is a song that had been passed down through the ages and it had never been written, so the words got changed while the melody stayed the same. Paladin helped with recovering the words that went to the melody.<br /><br />I believe this is the last book in the series, and the epilogue happens three years after the events throughout the rest of the book. I found it extremely engaging and I could not put it down, or did not want to put it down.<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I especially found it funny when Kale's baby Penn is born, and Fly, the protector dragon whom Kale thought was defective with no talent, is bonded to the baby and she forgives Kale for keeping her child trapped inside because "she can see I've [Kale had]done a fine job of taking care of him so far."  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="4672417564828350961" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_53741502" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/53741502" />
    <a title="Sandy Lender" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1199820-sandy-lender"><img alt="Sandy Lender" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442467211p2/1199820.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/53741502?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sandy Lender" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sandy Lender" href="/user/show/1199820-sandy-lender">Sandy Lender</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">young adults, adults</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Sandy by: </span>
      no one
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer53741502" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4373817512967938679">It's a little difficult to tell who the main character is, but I'm selecting Kale, the dragon keeper. Her husband, Bardon, vies for this position as the two head off on a quest to help their meech dragon friends Gilda and Reginor get to a legendary meech colony in the north where Gilda can present her egg. It's a cool quest. But there's bad stuff going on in their land. People calling themselves "Followers" are spreading a message contrary to Paladin's teachings. They think wizards like Kale and</span>
  <span id="freeText4373817512967938679" style="display:none">It's a little difficult to tell who the main character is, but I'm selecting Kale, the dragon keeper. Her husband, Bardon, vies for this position as the two head off on a quest to help their meech dragon friends Gilda and Reginor get to a legendary meech colony in the north where Gilda can present her egg. It's a cool quest. But there's bad stuff going on in their land. People calling themselves "Followers" are spreading a message contrary to Paladin's teachings. They think wizards like Kale and their dragons are to be destroyed. Between these con-artist-like Followers and clouds of dart-like, poisonous little black dragons, evil is closing in on Kale, Bardon, Gilda, Reginor, and the good people who work to help them.<br /><br />Packed with cute dragons doing cute dragon things and clever characters uncovering evildoers' plans, this story brings an old legend in the <i>DragonKeeper Chronicles</i> world to life and offers new visions as a compelling allegory for Christ's sacrifice. I was impressed with the climax to the story and know others will be, too. Even if you don't catch (or believe) the Salvation story, DragonLight offers a great story of friendship, loyalty, sacrifice, and the triumph of good over evil.<br /><br />I highly recommend <i>DragonLight</i> as a wonderful fantasy novel for young adults and adults alike. It isn't necessary to read the entire series to follow the action in this self-contained story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4373817512967938679" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14058020905086715351">The fantastic land of Amara is recovering from years of war inflicted on its citizens by outside forces–as well as from the spiritual apathy corroding the Amarans’ hearts. With Kale and her father serving as dragon keepers for Paladin, the dragon populace has exploded. It’s a peaceful, exciting time of rebuilding. And yet, an insidious, unseen evil lurks just beneath the surface of the idyllic countryside. <br/><br/>Truth has never been more important, nor so difficult to discern.<br/><br/>As Kale and her father ar</span>
  <span id="freeText14058020905086715351" style="display:none">The fantastic land of Amara is recovering from years of war inflicted on its citizens by outside forces–as well as from the spiritual apathy corroding the Amarans’ hearts. With Kale and her father serving as dragon keepers for Paladin, the dragon populace has exploded. It’s a peaceful, exciting time of rebuilding. And yet, an insidious, unseen evil lurks just beneath the surface of the idyllic countryside. <br /><br />Truth has never been more important, nor so difficult to discern.<br /><br />As Kale and her father are busy hatching, bonding, and releasing the younger generation of dragons as helpers throughout the kingdom, the light wizard has little time to develop her skills. Her husband, Sir Bardon–despite physical limitations resulting from his bout with the stakes disease–has become a leader, serving on the governing board under Paladin. When Kale and Bardon set aside their daily responsibilities to join meech dragons Regidor and Gilda on a quest to find a hidden meech colony, they encounter sinister forces. Their world is under attack by a secret enemy… can they overcome the ominous peril they can’t even see?<br /><br />Prepare to experience breathtaking adventure and mind-blowing fantasy as never before in this dazzling, beautifully-crafted conclusion to Donita K. Paul’s popular DragonKeeper Chronicles fantasy series.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('XCRbeQDTPXeO+waqSawdsjm35mQ5Kuq+TDcsWkGkfi1zauLE2YTsvgE6HytuaPFx4dsQcJJpHNn4JGzZ91387w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }
